# The Box That Came on a Tuesday

```meta
id: the-box-that-came-on-a-tuesday
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.8
scores: affirm 4 / emotion 3 / enjoy 4 / audio 4 / craft 4
words: 1286
minutes: ~10
date: 2026-06-04
source_chat: Powers that malfunction at awkward times
source_uuid: 8dd7e151-48dd-44de-8e3a-b12a22650075
prompt: Felix Alex Elfine and Marion new adventure, new owners, everyone gets a power that goes wrong at different times in the story they can be just awkward times rather than during a te
reviewed: yes (read/known)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
notes: Powers misfire at awkward (not tense) moments. Gentle.
```

## Story

The box arrived on a Tuesday, which everyone agreed was suspicious.

It was on the doorstep when Felix and Alex came back from the field. Medium-sized. Brown paper. Four names written on it in very neat handwriting:

**Felix. Alex. Elfine. Marion.**

"It's for all of us," said Felix.

"Elfine and Marion aren't here yet," said Alex.

"They'll be here in twenty minutes," said Felix. "We should probably wait."

There was a pause.

"We're not going to wait, are we," said Alex.

"We are absolutely not waiting," said Felix.

They waited. It was the longest twenty minutes of Felix's life.

---

Elfine and Marion arrived in a rush, coats still on, one of Marion's plaits half-undone from the car journey.

"Is that it?" said Elfine, pointing at the box.

"Yes," said Felix.

"Have you opened it?"

"We waited," said Alex.

Elfine looked at him. "You waited?"

"Twenty minutes," said Felix, with great suffering in his voice.

Marion was already reading the label. She was seven, which meant she read faster than both the boys, a fact she never mentioned but didn't hide either. "It says *New Owners,*" she said. "That's what it says instead of a return address. Just — *New Owners.*"

They all looked at each other.

Felix opened the box.

Inside were four smaller boxes, gold, with shifting question marks on the lids.

"Oh," said Alex quietly. He had seen boxes like this before. "Those are power boxes."

"Power boxes," Elfine repeated. She picked hers up and turned it over. "What kind of powers?"

"Different every time," said Felix, and opened his without another word.

---

Felix got **Super Speed**.

He immediately ran to the kitchen and back in half a second, skidded on the rug, crashed into the coat rack, knocked over three wellies and a umbrella, and ended up sitting on the floor looking pleased with himself.

"Brilliant," he said.

Alex got **the ability to talk to birds**.

He went to the window, looked at a pigeon on the fence, and said hello.

The pigeon said something back.

Alex went very still.

"What did it say?" said Marion.

"I'd rather not repeat it," said Alex. "Pigeons are quite rude, apparently."

Elfine got **the ability to make anything she touched glow softly**.

She touched the box. It glowed. She touched the windowsill. It glowed. She touched Marion's sleeve.

"Elfine!" said Marion, looking at her glowing arm.

"Sorry," said Elfine, who didn't look sorry at all.

Marion got **the ability to make things exactly the right size** — a bit like shrinking or growing, but more precise. She tested it on a crisp from the snack drawer. It became exactly the right size for one perfect bite.

"That's very useful," she said, and ate it.

---

They had all just agreed to go and investigate the old water tower on the edge of the fifteen-acre field — someone had nailed a sign to it that said PRIVATE (OCCUPIED) (PLEASE KNOCK) — when Felix's Super Speed went off by accident.

He didn't mean it. He sneezed.

WHOOOOOSH.

He was in the garden. Then the field. Then back in the garden. Then in the kitchen.

"FELIX!" shouted Mummy from upstairs.

"SORRY!" Felix shouted back, from five rooms away and then also immediately right behind her.

Mummy looked at him for a long moment.

"Tea," she said, to herself, and went downstairs.

Felix rejoined the others at a normal walking pace, holding his nose just in case.

---

The water tower did have someone in it.

When they knocked, a small hatch opened near the bottom and a nose appeared. The nose was attached to a face, and the face belonged to someone about the size of a large badger, with spectacles and a clipboard.

"Ah," said the face. "The new owners. Excellent. I've been waiting."

"Waiting for us specifically?" said Alex.

"For whoever opened the box. That's always been how it works." The hatch opened wider. Inside, the tower was surprisingly cosy — a round room, bookshelves on every curved wall, a kettle, and maps pinned everywhere. "I'm the Cartographer. I map things that don't want to be found. I've been mapping this field and forest for eleven years. I need someone to carry the findings to the town, because I can't leave the tower. My knees."

"What's wrong with your knees?" said Elfine.

"They've decided they prefer it in here." The Cartographer tapped his clipboard. "I have seventeen new maps. The fountain keeper's real name. Where the fox actually lives. The exact location of the stone bridge when it moves."

"The bridge moves?" said Felix.

"Occasionally. On Thursdays, usually."

Everyone filed in. Marion immediately spotted that the bookshelves were crooked and adjusted three of them to exactly the right angle while the Cartographer wasn't looking.

Alex sat next to the window. A starling landed on the outside sill and said something. Alex went slightly pink.

"Are birds always like that?" he whispered.

"What did it say?" said Marion.

"It said we smell like sandwiches."

"That's fair," said Elfine. "We did have sandwiches."

---

It was while the Cartographer was rolling up the first map for them to carry that Elfine's power went slightly wrong.

She was just resting her hand on the table. She wasn't even thinking about it.

The map started glowing.

Then the table.

Then the kettle.

Then, somehow, the Cartographer's spectacles.

"Oh dear," said the Cartographer, blinking through glowing lenses. He didn't seem annoyed. "That's quite festive, actually."

"I'm really sorry," said Elfine.

"Don't be. I've always thought this room needed atmosphere."

He looked around at his softly glowing bookshelves and glowing kettle and maps like lanterns and seemed, quietly, very pleased.

---

On the way back across the field, Marion's power went off twice.

First when she was thinking about the stone bridge — suddenly it became very small in her mind, and then the actual stone bridge at the bottom of the meadow became briefly the size of a shoe. They heard a small *clunk* from far away.

"Was that—" said Alex.

"I'll fix it when we get closer," said Marion, very calmly.

(She did.)

The second time was when Felix started running at normal speed and Marion thought *that's too fast* and he briefly became very small — about the size of a rabbit — took three more running steps, looked down at his feet in confusion, and then went back to normal.

"Did you do that?" said Felix.

"You were running too fast."

"I was running at normal speed!"

"For you, yes."

Felix thought about this. "Fair enough," he said.

---

They delivered the maps to Mrs. Okafor at the post office, who seemed to be expecting them. She put them straight in a drawer marked CARTOGRAPHER (CURRENT) as if there were older drawers with the same label, which there probably were.

On the way back, they stopped at the edge of the field where the afternoon was going golden.

"Same time next Tuesday?" said Elfine.

"There might be another box," said Marion.

Alex looked at the sky. A starling looked back.

He chose not to ask it anything.

"Same time next Tuesday," he said.

---

*Postscript: The Cartographer's spectacles kept a faint glow for three weeks. He told people it was a medical condition. Nobody questioned it.*

*Postscript: Felix sneezed twice more on the walk home. On the second one he ended up briefly in the bakery. Mr. Pemberton handed him a sausage roll without looking up.*

*Postscript: The stone bridge was entirely normal on Thursday. Nobody mentioned the shoe incident. The Grumble under it had not noticed, or had decided not to say anything, which is much more likely.*

*[END]*


===STORY===

# Winchester and the Villainette

```meta
id: winchester-and-the-villainette
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.797
scores: affirm 3.75 / emotion 3.29 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 4.58
words: 1399
minutes: ~10
date: 2026-06-19
source_chat: Winchester the teddy bear and laser tag guns
source_uuid: 06095567-b992-4d58-9ffb-011245ae304d
prompt: another story with Winchester Vs a villain villainette (Felix named her), and they get some powers (unspecified could be big or small)   Keep it under 1500 words
reviewed: auto-scored (confirm on read)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
```

## Story

The boxes appeared on Saturday morning.

Three of them, small and gold, sitting on the kitchen table next to the cereal bowls. Winchester was already up — Winchester woke very early on weekends, because there was so much to see — and he was standing on his chair examining them carefully with his wonky ear pointing forward.

"Powers," said Felix, who knew what gold boxes meant.

"Powers," confirmed Winchester, nodding seriously, as though he had seen many gold boxes in his time and this was exactly the right response.

Alex looked at all three boxes. One for Felix. One for Alex. One for Winchester, which had a little bow on it, because whoever sent powers had excellent manners.

They opened them at the same time.

Felix got *Mega Bounce* — he could jump extremely high, as high as he wanted, and land perfectly every time. He immediately jumped and hit the kitchen ceiling. "BRILLIANT," he announced, from up there.

Alex got *Slow Down* — he could make things move at half speed just by looking at them hard. He tried it on Felix's cereal, and the splashing milk went dreamy and slow in mid-air. "Oh," Alex said quietly. "That's very useful."

Winchester opened his box and found a small pair of *rocket boots* — which, on a bear the size of a teapot, looked very funny and went very fast. He strapped them on. He zoomed immediately into the fridge. "I meant to do that," he said, from inside the fridge.

But before any of them could practice properly, there was a knock at the door.

A very small, very cross knock.

Felix answered it. On the doorstep stood a girl. She was perhaps six years old, with enormous eyebrows pulled into an enormous frown, wearing a purple cloak that was slightly too big and dragging on the path. In one hand she held a wand. In the other she held a list.

"I," she announced, "am Millicent. And I have come to collect the sunshine."

"Sorry?" said Alex.

Millicent held up her list. It was written in very neat handwriting, because Millicent was nothing if not organised. "Item one. The morning sunshine over the back field. I'm taking it. I need it for my plans."

"What plans?" said Alex.

"*Villain* plans," said Millicent, and looked very satisfied with herself.

Felix stared at her. She was very small and very certain and her cloak had a small badge on it that said *TRAINEE* in gold letters.

"She's a *villainette*," Felix breathed, delighted.

Millicent drew herself up to her full height, which was not very much. "I prefer—"

"A VILLAINETTE," Felix said again, even more delighted. "Alex, she's a villainette. That's what you call a villain who's still learning. I just decided."

Millicent's enormous eyebrows went even higher. She looked like she might argue. Then she looked like she was considering it. Then, very grudgingly: "That's actually quite a good word."

"Thank you," said Felix.

"It doesn't mean I'm not taking the sunshine," said Millicent.

And here was the thing: she *was* taking it. Behind her, out in the back field, the lovely Saturday morning was going grey and flat, the gold being hoovered out of it by a small spinning device Millicent had placed by the fence. It made a sound like WHRRRRR-SLURP-WHRRRR, and the sunshine was rolling into it like a carpet being wound up.

Without sunshine, the field went the colour of a Monday. The grass looked tired. A rabbit came out of a burrow, looked at the sky, and went straight back in.

Winchester rocketed past Felix's head on his boots. "I'll assess the device," he called, zooming out across the field.

"Alex," said Felix, "can you slow down that machine?"

Alex looked at the whirring device across the field. He squinted. He concentrated. The machine didn't stop — his power was Slow Down, not Stop — but it went half speed, buying them time. WHRRRRRR became whrrrrrrr, drowsy and slow. The sunshine stopped moving.

Felix turned back to Millicent.

"Why do you need it?" he said. Not fierce. Just asking. Because Felix always asked.

Millicent's enormous eyebrows did something complicated. She pulled her cloak tighter. "My greenhouse," she said finally, stiffly, like it cost her something. "My tomatoes won't grow. I've tried everything. They need more sun and there isn't enough and I've been growing them since March and they're still *green* and it's not *fair*."

Felix and Alex looked at each other.

Alex said nothing, because that was Alex's way when something sad had just arrived.

Felix said: "You could have just asked for help."

Millicent blinked. This had clearly not occurred to her. She had gone straight to *villain plans* without stopping at *asking nicely*, which was a route many people took but which never worked as well.

Winchester flew back across the field and hovered at Felix's shoulder level. "The machine can be reversed," he said. "One good jump would do it. Land right on that red button."

Felix looked at the machine. He looked at the field. He looked up at the sky, measuring.

He jumped.

It was an extraordinary jump — the kind that made even the rabbit come back out of its burrow to watch — a great soaring arc over the grey flat field, and Felix came down right on the red button with a CLANG that rang out across the countryside.

WHRRRRR-SLURP went the machine, but backwards now. And the sunshine came rolling back out across the field like a carpet being unrolled, gold and warm, spreading all the way to the fence and over it and into the garden and up the side of the house.

The rabbit sat in it and looked very pleased.

Millicent stood very still. Her list fluttered in the breeze.

"There's actually loads of sunshine," Felix said, landing next to her. "The field has tons. You don't need to take it. You could just — ask it nicely. Things in the countryside share if you ask."

"Sunshine doesn't listen," said Millicent.

"Lots of things listen if you're quiet enough," said Alex, and looked at her steadily.

Millicent looked at the field. She looked at her list. She folded it up slowly and put it in her cloak pocket. The trainee badge caught the light.

"My tomatoes are very small," she said quietly.

"We know someone with a glasshouse," said Felix. "On the hill. She's called Miriam and she knows everything about growing things and I've painted her walls and she gives you biscuits when you visit. I could take you."

Millicent considered this for a long moment. Her eyebrows, at rest, were really quite normal eyebrows. She had just been pulling them into a frown so long it had started to feel like her face.

"I suppose," she said, very carefully, "a villainette can take a break."

"You can have the word," Felix told her. "Even if you stop being one. It'll still be yours."

That made Millicent smile. It was a small smile, because she was out of practice, but it was there.

Winchester landed neatly on the fence post and folded his arms with enormous dignity, which was difficult in rocket boots but he managed it.

"Case closed," he said.

*The End.*

---

**Postscripts:**

*Millicent visited Miriam's glasshouse on Sunday afternoon. Miriam gave her a spot in the corner near the warm pipe. The tomatoes, Felix reports, are already looking more cheerful.*

*The gold boxes left no note, as usual. Winchester suspects he knows who sends them. He hasn't said.*

*Felix wrote VILLAINETTE in big letters on a piece of paper and stuck it on the fridge. He says it should be a real word. Alex looked it up. It isn't yet. Felix is not discouraged.*

---

**Affirmations woven through:**
- *Ask before you take* — Millicent's whole problem was skipping asking and going straight to scheming
- *Asking is braver than taking* — Felix says it plainly, the way he always does
- *Things share if you ask nicely* — the countryside principle, now canon for this universe too
- *You can change direction* — a villainette can take a break, and the word is still hers

Want Millicent to come back? She's got good bones — organised, determined, deeply silly, sad underneath. Classic Thursday group energy, though she's not quite ready yet.

*[END]*


===STORY===

# The Metal Singers

```meta
id: the-metal-singers
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.792
scores: affirm 5 / emotion 1.8 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 3.61
words: 1881
minutes: ~14
date: 2025-12-18
source_chat: The crystal garden discovery
source_uuid: 2ea738f1-f119-4702-a6e8-0614d724352b
prompt: Please tell us another story. Maybe a new story with new powers like the push and pull powers of Mistborn.
reviewed: auto-scored (confirm on read)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
```

## Story

Felix was helping his dad organize the garage on Saturday morning when he heard it - a strange humming sound coming from the crystal garden. But this wasn't Theo's musical humming. This sounded like metal singing.

"That's weird," Felix muttered, putting down the toolbox he'd been carrying. The humming got louder, and some of the wrenches in the toolbox started to vibrate gently.

He ran outside to find Alex, Violet, and Theo all staring at two new crystals that had appeared overnight near the oak tree. One crystal was dark gray like iron and seemed to be pulling at every metal object in the yard - the garden gate was creaking as it swayed toward the crystal, and even the metal buttons on Theo's overalls were tugging forward.

The other crystal was bright silver like polished steel, and it was doing the opposite - pushing metal things away. The wind chimes on the porch were being gently shoved back and forth, and Dad's metal watering can had somehow slid all the way to the far end of the garden.

"Don't touch them yet!" Violet called as Felix approached. Her purple crystal was glowing as she tried to sense what these new crystals were feeling. "They're... they're really excited about something, but also kind of dangerous."

Just then, their friends came running up the driveway - but they looked alarmed instead of excited for their usual Saturday practice.

"Did you guys feel that?" Emily panted, her yellow crystal flickering. "Every metal thing in town started humming at the same time! The birds are going crazy because all the metal bird feeders are vibrating!"

"And look!" Winter held up her white crystal, which was glowing urgently. "My ice magic can sense that these aren't just any crystals. They're connected to every piece of metal for miles around!"

Aria's pink healing crystal was warm with concern. "I can feel that they're powerful, but they're also... impatient? Like they've been waiting a really long time for someone to use them properly."

Felix studied the two new crystals carefully. The iron-gray one seemed to be calling to him, whispering that he could pull any metal object toward himself. The steel-silver one hummed with the promise that he could push metal things away with just a thought.

"It's like the old stories Garrett tells us," he realized. "About metal-magic that lets you push and pull on iron and steel!"

Veer's orange crystal was tingling in his hand. "What if we could push and pull on metal to move ourselves around? Like... using the metal fence posts to launch yourself across the yard?"

"Or pulling on that metal weather vane to zip up to the roof?" Alex added, her silver wind crystal showing her how the metal objects could work with air currents.

"That sounds really dangerous," Violet said, but Felix could see the curiosity in her eyes.

"Everything's dangerous until we learn how to do it safely," Felix pointed out. "Remember when I first got my speed and flight crystals?"

They decided to start very, very carefully. Felix knelt down between the two crystals but didn't touch them yet.

"What if only one of us tries the metal magic first?" he suggested. "And everyone else stays ready to help if something goes wrong?"

"Why you?" Alex asked. "Maybe I should try since my wind magic already helps me understand movement through the air?"

"Or me," said Veer, "since my size magic means I understand changing how objects behave?"

But when Felix held his hands out over both crystals without quite touching them, something interesting happened. His green plant crystal started to glow warmly, and he could sense what the metal crystals were trying to tell him.

"They want someone who already knows how to be connected to a big network," he said slowly. "My plant magic connects me to all the roots and growing things for miles. These crystals want to connect me to all the metal objects for miles, but they need me to already understand what that kind of connection feels like."

"So you're like... the right person to learn this safely?" Emily asked.

Felix nodded. "I think so. But I'm not doing this alone." He looked around at all his friends and family. "Everyone needs to be ready to help, just like always."

Very carefully, Felix placed his left hand on the iron crystal and his right hand on the steel crystal. Immediately, he could feel every piece of metal in their entire neighborhood - every nail in every house, every car engine, every metal fence post, every kitchen knife, every bicycle chain.

"Whoa," he breathed. "This is... this is a lot."

"What do you feel?" Violet asked, her purple crystal helping her sense Felix's amazement and slight overwhelm.

"Everything metal," Felix said. "I can feel the car keys in Mom's purse inside the house. I can feel the metal playground equipment at school two miles away. I can feel... oh wow, I can feel the metal bridge over Miller's Creek!"

Alex watched with her wind magic as the air around Felix began to shimmer slightly. "You're not just feeling the metal - you're connected to it somehow!"

Felix concentrated on the smallest piece of metal he could sense - a paperclip on the ground near his feet. Instead of reaching for it with his hands, he tried gently pulling on it with the iron crystal's power.

The paperclip slid smoothly across the ground toward him.

"It worked!" Theo clapped his hands, making celebration flowers bloom around them.

"Now try pushing something away," suggested Winter.

Felix focused on his dad's empty metal watering can at the edge of the garden. Very gently, he tried pushing it with the steel crystal's power. The watering can glided smoothly away from him until it bumped softly against the fence.

"This is incredible," Felix said. "But I can feel how easy it would be to push or pull too hard and send things flying."

That's when Violet had an important realization. "Felix, what if this isn't just about moving metal objects around? What if it's about using metal objects to move yourself?"

Felix blinked. "What do you mean?"

"Think about it," Violet continued, her purple crystal helping her understand the deeper possibilities. "If you can pull on that metal fence post, instead of pulling it toward you, what if you pull yourself toward it?"

Felix looked at the sturdy metal fence post about ten feet away. Very carefully, he tried pulling on it - but instead of trying to make it come to him, he tried to make himself go to it.

Suddenly, he slid smoothly across the grass toward the fence post, as if he were on invisible skates!

"Felix!" Alex gasped. "You're metal-skating!"

"This is the coolest thing ever," Emily laughed, as her yellow crystal translated the excited chirping of birds who were watching from the trees.

For the next hour, Felix practiced his new metal magic while his friends and family helped keep him safe. He learned that he could pull himself toward large metal objects like fence posts and playground equipment. He could push against metal things to change his direction while sliding. And most amazingly, he could use both powers together - pushing off one metal object while pulling toward another - to almost fly through the air, as long as there was metal for him to push and pull against.

"It's like you're dancing with the metal world," Alex observed, watching how smoothly Felix moved between the various metal objects in their yard.

But the real excitement came when they realized this could be another team magic opportunity.

"Felix," Violet said thoughtfully, "what if you could carry some of our magic with you when you're metal-sliding around?"

Working together, they discovered that Felix could carry small amounts of everyone's magic while using his push-pull powers. He could zip around the property at amazing speeds, carrying Alex's wind magic to places that needed a cooling breeze, delivering Aria's healing magic to plants that were hurt, bringing Emily's animal-communication magic to creatures who were too far away to talk to normally, and even transporting some of Theo's musical magic to make flowers bloom in perfect patterns.

"We're like a magical postal service!" Veer laughed.

"Better than that," said Alex. "We're like... magical emergency responders! Felix can get anywhere fast and bring exactly the right kind of help!"

They were so busy practicing and having fun that they didn't notice Garrett approaching until they heard his gentle thunder-voice.

"Push and pull magic!" the giant said admiringly, shrinking down to people size. "I haven't seen that in decades!"

"Have you used this kind of magic before?" Felix asked, landing gracefully after pulling himself along a series of metal fence posts.

"When I was very young, before I learned size magic," Garrett nodded. "But I could never master it the way you're already learning to. Push-pull magic requires incredible focus and spatial awareness. Most people who try it end up launching themselves into trees or pulling heavy objects down on their heads."

"How is Felix learning it so safely then?" Winter asked.

Garrett smiled. "Because he's not learning it alone. Metal magic is dangerous when someone tries to show off or be independent. But Felix is using it as part of your team's cooperation, not as a way to be more powerful than everyone else."

Felix nodded, placing his hands back on the two crystals. "It doesn't feel like my magic," he said. "It feels like our magic that I happen to be the one channeling."

"And," added Violet, "his connection to plant networks taught him how to handle being connected to lots of things at once. He already knew how to be part of a big system without getting overwhelmed."

As the afternoon sun started to set, they practiced one final combination of all their magics together. Felix used his metal magic to zip in complex patterns around the garden while carrying everyone else's abilities with him. Theo's musical flowers bloomed in spirals, Alex's wind created dancing ribbons of air, Winter's gentle ice made temporary stepping stones, Aria's healing magic refreshed every plant he passed, Emily's animal communication brought curious rabbits and birds to watch, Veer's size magic made some flowers tiny and others large, and Violet's emotional coordination made it all flow together like a beautiful, magical dance.

When they were finished, they all sat together under the oak tree, tired but happy.

"I think," said Felix, "this might be our most complicated magic yet."

"But also our most connected," Alex added. "Every time we get new abilities, we get better at working together."

Garrett nodded approvingly. "That's the sign of true magical wisdom - when new power makes you more united rather than more individual."

As they gathered up their things to head inside for dinner, Felix took one last look at the iron and steel crystals, now glowing softly in the evening light.

"Tomorrow," he said to them quietly, "we'll learn even more about working together."

The crystals hummed gently in response, and every piece of metal in the neighborhood seemed to hum along in harmony, like a great big metallic choir welcoming their newest conductor.

---

*The End!*

*[END]*


===STORY===

# The Iron Forest

```meta
id: the-iron-forest
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.697
scores: affirm 4.25 / emotion 1.84 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 4.68
words: 1454
minutes: ~11
date: 2026-06-19
source_chat: Winchester the teddy bear and laser tag guns
source_uuid: 06095567-b992-4d58-9ffb-011245ae304d
prompt: another story please, Felix Alex Elfine Marion, they get powers and can vote to swap, but everyone has to agree to the swap you don't always have to share if you don't want to. und
reviewed: auto-scored (confirm on read)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
```

## Story

Elfine and Marion arrived on Saturday morning with a bag each, matching wellies, and the very particular energy of seven-year-olds who had been in a car for two hours and were ready to be somewhere that wasn't a car.

"RIGHT," said Elfine, dumping her bag in the hall. "What's the plan?"

"The forest," said Felix immediately.

"Obviously the forest," said Marion.

Alex was already at the back door with his boots on.

Four gold boxes were sitting on the garden wall.

Felix went straight for his. "POWERS," he said.

"We know," said Marion, who had heard about the boxes before. She picked hers up with great care, as if it might be alive, which it might have been.

They opened them together.

Felix got *Iron Sense* — he could feel metal underground, like a compass but in his whole body. Old iron, deep in the earth. He stood up and immediately turned in a slow circle. "There's something that way," he said, pointing toward the forest. "Something old."

Alex got *Echo Listen* — he could hear sounds from the past if he pressed his ear to the right surface. Stone, bark, very old wood. Things that had absorbed a long time.

Elfine got *Trail Finder* — her feet knew the right path, even where there wasn't one. She could find where people had walked before, even centuries ago.

Marion got *Fire Memory* — she could see the ghost of old fires. Not dangerous, not hot. Just the shape and light of them, hovering where they'd once burned.

They looked at each other.

"Can we swap?" said Felix immediately. He wanted Echo Listen.

"We can vote," said Alex. "But everyone has to say yes."

"What's the rule?" said Elfine.

"Everyone agrees, or it doesn't happen," said Alex. "You don't have to share if you don't want to."

Marion was already shaking her head. "I'm keeping Fire Memory. It sounds brilliant."

"Fair enough," said Felix, who actually wanted to keep his own anyway. He could already feel something pulling at him from across the fifteen-acre field. Old iron, very old, deep and patient.

"Let's just go," said Elfine, and her feet were already pointing toward the forest path as if they'd decided on their own.

---

The forest was cool and green and smelled of bark and damp earth. The paths crossed back and forth through the trees, and you could walk for twenty minutes and feel completely alone, with only bird sounds and the rush of a stream somewhere below.

Felix walked like a dowsing rod. "This way," he kept saying, tugging slightly left, slightly forward, down toward the slope where the trees grew older and closer.

"I'm getting something," said Elfine, picking up her pace. "There was a path here. A *really* old one. My feet can feel it."

"What does it feel like?" said Marion.

"Like the ground remembers being walked on," said Elfine. "Loads of times. Hundreds of years of times."

They followed the ghost-path down the slope. And then Alex stopped.

He pressed his palm flat against an old oak.

He went very still.

"What?" said Felix.

"Hammering," said Alex quietly. "I can hear it. Like — metal on metal. Really fast and really loud. But far away. Like hearing something through water."

"*Old* hammering?" said Elfine.

"Very old," said Alex. He took his hand away. The sound stopped. He looked a bit awed. "There were people here," he said. "Working. Lots of them."

---

At the bottom of the slope, the land flattened out around a long dark pond. It was quiet now, reeds at one end, a duck who did not seem impressed by visitors.

Marion stopped walking.

Her eyes had gone very round.

"What?" said Elfine.

"The fire," Marion breathed. "The fire memory — there's fire *everywhere* down here. Big fires. All around the edge of the pond. Big round ones, like — like mounds of fire, but old, like the colour of something that happened a long time ago."

"Charcoal fires," said Felix, who suddenly knew this the way you know things when your whole body is a compass for something ancient. "They burned the wood down here. To make charcoal. To smelt the iron."

"How do you know that word?" said Marion. "Smelt?"

"I don't know," said Felix. "I just do. The iron's telling me."

He crouched down near the edge of the pond. The soil near the bank was dark — not mud-dark but char-dark, nearly black in places, with small pieces of something in it like tiny black glass.

Alex crouched too. He pressed two fingers into the dark earth.

"Charcoal," said Alex. "Someone made charcoal right here. They'd have lived here too, while the fires were going. Built a little shelter. Watched the fires all night."

"In the forest," said Elfine softly. "In the dark. All night."

"That's brilliant," said Felix.

"That's terrifying," said Marion. But she was grinning.

---

They found the hollow way on the way back. Elfine's feet stopped her at a dip in the ground that ran between two trees, worn down below the level of the forest floor. Not a stream — no water. Just a deep worn groove in the earth, as if something very heavy had passed this way many hundreds of times.

"Old road," said Elfine. "My feet *love* this. They want to walk it."

They all walked it. Single file, between the rising banks, the forest on either side. Felix felt the iron sense change as they walked — less deep, more spread out, like something had been carried along this path many times.

"They would have brought the iron ore down here," he said. "Bags of it. On carts maybe. To the furnace."

"There'd have been a furnace pond somewhere," said Alex. "To power the hammers." He looked at the long dark pond behind them. "Oh," he said.

Marion turned and looked at it properly. Afternoon light through the trees.

"That's not a normal pond," she said. "Is it."

"I don't think it ever was," said Felix.

---

They made it back to the house at teatime, very muddy, extremely happy, with dark soil on their knees and small pieces of what might have been very old slag in Felix's pocket, which Mummy looked at and did not comment on.

Robert came in from somewhere, saw four filthy children at the back door, and put the kettle on.

"Find anything?" he said.

"A charcoal burning place," said Felix. "And a hammer pond. And a road that's been a road for five hundred years."

"And fires," said Marion. "I could see the fires."

Robert handed four mugs of hot chocolate to four muddy children.

"The forest," he said, "has been the forest for a very long time." He looked out the window at the trees on the hill. "More of it under there than above it, if you know how to look."

Felix looked at the forest too.

He could still feel the iron.

It went on for miles.

*The End.*

---

**Postscripts:**

*The piece of slag in Felix's pocket is now on the evidence shelf, between the echo jar and Arthur's Mondays. It is not labelled yet. Felix says everyone will know what it is.*

*Marion keeps trying to see fire memory in the kitchen. So far she has found: the ghost of a very old candle, and what might be the memory of a particularly good bonfire from three years ago.*

*Elfine's feet took her down the hollow way again on Sunday. She walked it all the way to the edge of the forest and back. She says it feels like the path is glad to be walked.*

*Alex pressed his ear against the old oak again on their way out. He heard the hammering. He didn't tell the others this time. Some things are just for keeping.*

---

**What's real in your forest (and actually there to find):**
- Nearly black soil with tiny charcoal pieces = charcoal burning platform
- A pond that looks slightly too regular = probably a hammer pond or furnace pond
- A worn groove running between old trees going downhill = hollow way, used for centuries
- Brown-stained water in a stream = iron ore in the ground nearby
- A slightly flattened circular area in the trees = where a charcoal burner's hut stood

**Affirmations woven through:**
- *You don't always have to share — but when you do, you do it by agreement*
- *Knowing how to look changes what you see*
- *Old things aren't gone, they're just waiting to be found*
- *Being somewhere properly — slowly, quietly, with attention — is its own kind of power*

*[END]*


===STORY===

# The Time-Keeper's Garden

```meta
id: the-time-keepers-garden
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.668
scores: affirm 5 / emotion 2.24 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 2.2
words: 1211
minutes: ~9
date: 2025-12-18
source_chat: Felix and the crystal singers
source_uuid: 9fcda924-f978-41a4-814a-8a919c91ad83
prompt: Can we have another story where Felix can talk to clocks, control time, communicate with animals, and they find dinosaurs, real live ones that are friendly.
reviewed: auto-scored (confirm on read)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
```

## Story

Felix was helping his parents clean out the attic when he found the strangest pocket watch he'd ever seen. It was made of what looked like crystal and copper, and instead of numbers, it had tiny carved animals around the clock face—a T-Rex at twelve o'clock, a triceratops at three, a stegosaurus at six, and a pterodactyl at nine.

The moment Felix touched it, the watch began to tick very loudly, and then something incredible happened—it started talking to him!

"Oh my gears and springs!" chimed a tiny, cheerful voice. "Finally! Someone who can hear me! I'm Chronos, and I've been waiting up here for seventy-three years, four months, two weeks, and six days!"

Felix nearly dropped the watch. "You can talk?"

"Of course I can talk! I'm a Time-Keeper's watch! And judging by the fact that you can hear me, you must have temporal abilities. Time magic, my boy! Very rare indeed!"

Felix discovered that not only could he talk to Chronos, but he could talk to every clock in the house. The grandfather clock in the hallway had a deep, wise voice. The kitchen timer was peppy and energetic. Even his digital alarm clock had a buzzing, electronic way of speaking.

But the real magic happened when Chronos taught Felix how to use his time abilities. By turning the watch's hands backward, Felix could slow down time around himself, making everything else move like thick honey while he moved normally. By spinning the hands forward, he could speed up his own time, making himself move super fast while everything else seemed frozen.

"But the best part," Chronos explained excitedly, "is that this watch is actually a key! It opens doorways to places where time works differently. And I happen to know of a very special place indeed!"

Felix couldn't wait to show his friends. He raced to the Whispering Woods where Emily, Winter, Aria, Veer, Theo, and Violet were playing near the crystal stones.

"Guys! Look at this!" Felix held up Chronos, who immediately began chattering excitedly to everyone, though only Felix could understand him.

"Your watch is talking," Theo said matter-of-factly. "I can hear a tiny voice but I can't understand what it's saying."

Chronos whispered instructions to Felix. "Tell them to gather around you, hold hands, and trust the magic. We're going somewhere wonderful!"

Felix explained what Chronos wanted, and his friends eagerly formed a circle. Felix held the pocket watch high and turned its hands in a special pattern Chronos had taught him. The world around them began to shimmer and swirl, like looking through water.

When everything stopped spinning, they found themselves in the most amazing place they'd ever seen. They were still in a forest, but everything was different. The trees were enormous, with thick trunks and strange, feathery leaves. Colorful flowers the size of dinner plates bloomed everywhere. And the air was warm and humid, filled with the sounds of unfamiliar animals.

"Welcome," Chronos announced proudly, "to the Time Garden! This is a pocket of the ancient world that I've been protecting for millions of years. Time moves differently here, which is why—"

His explanation was interrupted by a loud, friendly "SQUAWK!" from above. Looking up, they saw a bright green pterodactyl landing gracefully on a nearby branch. But instead of being scary, it tilted its head curiously and made soft, welcoming sounds.

"Oh wow," breathed Veer, who'd always been good with animals. "I think it's trying to say hello!"

Felix had an idea. He focused on his new time abilities and whispered to Chronos, "Can you help me understand what it's saying?"

The watch ticked thoughtfully. "Temporal translation, coming right up!"

Suddenly, Felix could understand the pterodactyl perfectly! "She says her name is Skywhisper, and she's been waiting for visitors who could appreciate the Time Garden without trying to hurt anyone!"

More friendly sounds came from the forest around them. A baby triceratops emerged from behind a tree, followed by its patient mother. Both dinosaurs moved slowly and gently, clearly curious about the children but not threatening at all.

"They're beautiful," whispered Emily, reaching out slowly toward the baby triceratops. To everyone's amazement, the little dinosaur nuzzled her hand like a friendly puppy.

Chronos explained that in the Time Garden, all the dinosaurs had evolved to be peaceful and intelligent. "Millions of years of protected time have let them develop into the gentle creatures they always had the potential to become."

Felix spent the afternoon using his time abilities to help his friends experience amazing things. He slowed down time so they could watch a family of tiny compsognathus dinosaurs building an intricate nest, each movement precise and careful. He sped up time around a patch of prehistoric flowers so they could watch them bloom in seconds instead of hours.

But the most wonderful discovery came when a wise old brachiosaurus approached their group. This dinosaur was enormous but moved with incredible gentleness. When it lowered its massive head toward Felix, Chronos began ticking excitedly.

"She's asking if you'd like to learn the Song of Deep Time," the watch translated. "It's a melody that dinosaurs have been singing for millions of years—a song that helps time flow peacefully and protects special places like this."

The brachiosaurus began to sing, and it was the most beautiful sound Felix had ever heard—deep and resonant, like the Earth itself was humming. With Chronos's help, Felix found he could understand the melody and sing along.

As he sang the Song of Deep Time with the ancient dinosaur, Felix felt his time abilities growing stronger and more gentle. He could sense the flow of time like a river, and he could help guide it to protect the things he cared about. When a butterfly landed on Violet's nose, Felix instinctively slowed time around it so it could rest safely. When Theo wanted to examine a fascinating prehistoric fern, Felix sped up its growth just enough for them to see how its leaves unfurled.

"The Song of Deep Time isn't about controlling time," Felix realized as the brachiosaurus finished her melody. "It's about understanding time and working with it to keep special moments and special places safe."

As the day in the Time Garden came to an end, Skywhisper the pterodactyl gave each child a beautiful, iridescent feather that shimmered with all the colors of sunset. The baby triceratops nuzzled each of them goodbye. And the wise brachiosaurus sang a soft farewell melody.

"We can come back anytime," Chronos promised as Felix used the watch to open the doorway home. "The Time Garden exists outside of normal time, so it's always here when you need it."

Back in their own world, Felix looked at his friends holding their pterodactyl feathers and grinned. "So now I can talk to clocks, work with time, understand any animal, and visit dinosaurs whenever we want. Not bad for finding an old watch in the attic!"

Winter examined her feather thoughtfully. "Do you think there are other time-protected places out there?"

Chronos ticked mysteriously. "Oh, my dear children, the universe is full of wonders hidden in the folds of time. And now that Felix is a true Time-Keeper, we have all the time in the world to find them!"

*[END]*

# Alex's Giggle Garden

```meta
id: alexs-giggle-garden
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.65
scores: affirm 4 / emotion 4 / enjoy 4 / audio 2 / craft 3
words: 232
minutes: ~2
date: 2026-01-20
source_chat: Story about Felix's joy with his cousins and Peter
source_uuid: f1970aa0-cc3f-4a05-a30d-b2682c9424a5
prompt: You tell me another story, but where Alex is the focus, and he feels joy about something different in
reviewed: yes (read/known)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
notes: Short voice-mode; emotion-focused. Slight.
```

## Story

One sunny afternoon, Alex was digging in the dirt behind their countryside house when he found something sparkly buried in the soil.

"FELIX! FELIX! Come quick!" Alex shouted.

Felix ran over, and there in Alex's hand was a tiny, glowing pebble. It was warm and hummed a little song!

"That's MAGIC!" gasped Felix.

Soon **Theo and Violet** came running. Then their cousins **Elfine and Marion** arrived on their scooters.

"We should plant it!" suggested Violet, who loved gardens.

So they dug a hole together and gently placed the humming pebble deep in the earth. Alex sprinkled water on it and—

**SPROOOOING!**

Up popped the silliest flowers anyone had ever seen! They were purple and orange striped, and they giggled when you tickled them. They smelled like pancakes and birthday cake!

**Alex felt JOY!** Pure, wonderful joy! His eyes got sparkly, and he laughed so hard he fell backwards into the grass. "I GREW GIGGLE FLOWERS! ME! ALEX!" He couldn't believe it was real.

Felix felt **amazed and proud** of his brother for finding the magic pebble.

Theo felt **curious**, gently touching the giggling flowers.

Violet felt **happy** because her garden idea worked perfectly.

Elfine and Marion felt **impressed** that Alex discovered something SO magical.

They all danced around the giggle garden, and every time one of them laughed, the flowers giggled back louder and louder!

*The End!* 🌸✨

*[END]*

# Sergeant Sticky Pants and the Terrible, Wonderful, Very Sticky Problem

```meta
id: sergeant-sticky-pants-and-the-terrible-wonderful-very-sticky-problem
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.65
scores: affirm 3 / emotion 3 / enjoy 5 / audio 4 / craft 4
words: 1617
minutes: ~12
date: 2026-06-05
source_chat: Sergeant Sticky Pants' next adventure
source_uuid: f067fe80-0499-46a6-9716-0d05696d8e78
prompt: new story, with a superhero, sergeant sticky pants who wears pants made from sugar. he accidentally turned his sidekick into a unicorn during a particularly hairy adventure.   now 
reviewed: yes (read/known)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
notes: Very silly, high fun, lighter affirmation. Comic palate-cleanser.
```

## Story

It started, as most excellent things do, with something landing in the field.

Felix saw it first. He was standing at the kitchen window eating a piece of toast — the kind with the crusts that curl up into small boats — when something fell out of the sky and went **FWUMP** into the long grass near the stone bridge.

"Alex," he said. "Something fell out of the sky."

Alex, who was sitting at the table and had been watching it for thirty seconds already, said, "I know. It looked sticky."

They pulled on their wellies (Felix's were on the wrong feet, which he preferred) and ran.

---

In the long grass, looking somewhat crumpled, was a man.

He was wearing a cape — bright yellow, with a sugar-spun 'S' on the back. His trousers were extraordinary. They appeared to be made of toffee. Not toffee-coloured. Actual toffee. They were currently stuck to three blades of grass and a small confused beetle.

"HALLO," said Felix.

The man peered up. He had a very fine moustache, slightly damp, and an extremely serious expression that would have been more convincing if a grass blade wasn't stuck to his forehead.

"I am Sergeant Sticky Pants," he said, "and I am on a mission. Please do not step on me."

"We weren't going to," said Alex, which was true.

"Is that your unicorn?" said Felix, pointing.

---

Standing ten feet away, nibbling a dandelion with great dignity, was a unicorn. It was white. It had a horn the colour of barley sugar. It was wearing a small utility belt.

"That," said Sergeant Sticky Pants, peeling himself from the grass with a sound like a very long piece of tape, "is my sidekick, Corporal Crisp. We were in the middle of a hairy adventure involving a rogue sprinkle cannon and a quantity of hardening caramel when I accidentally—"

"Turned him into a unicorn?" said Alex.

The Sergeant looked at him. "How did you know?"

Alex pointed at the utility belt. "It's got his name on it. And he looks embarrassed."

Corporal Crisp, who was the kind of unicorn that made embarrassment look dignified, flicked his tail once and went back to the dandelion.

"He won't turn back," said Sergeant Sticky Pants. "And I've tried everything. I tried the untransformation spray. I tried saying sorry four times while standing on one leg. I tried—" he reached into his cape, "—this."

He produced a small golden card. It said, in neat writing:

**IN CASE OF MAGICAL MISHAPS: SEEK THE BOYS IN THE FIELD.**

Felix and Alex looked at each other.

"That's us," said Felix. "We're the boys in the field."

"Yes," said Sergeant Sticky Pants. "Are you able to help?"

"Probably," said Felix.

"Definitely," said Alex, who had already started thinking.

---

Daddy was on the doorstep in his dressing gown. He watched two five-year-olds, a man in toffee trousers, and a unicorn walk up through the field towards the house.

He went inside and put the kettle on.

When they came in, he handed the Sergeant a mug without being asked, looked at the unicorn (who fit in the kitchen, barely), and said, "Sugar? Actually, never mind."

Sergeant Sticky Pants sat at the kitchen table and explained. His name was Gerald. The toffee trousers were a gift from his grandmother, who had been a confectioner and also somewhat magical. The trousers stuck to evil things, which had been very useful in his career. His sidekick had been called Nigel before the accident, and was still called Nigel, but now also happened to be a unicorn. And the problem with the un-transformation was that the wrong kind of magic had been used — the sticky kind, which hardened over time — and now the only thing that could unstick it was something that had never been stuck in the first place.

"Something that's never been stuck," said Felix.

"Exactly," said the Sergeant.

Felix looked at Alex.

Alex said, quietly, "The fountain."

---

Mrs. Okafor was not surprised to see them. She was often not surprised. She handed over the post without comment, gave Felix and Alex each a lemon sherbet, and said, "The fountain keeper's in a mood today. Don't feed it anything from Gerald's trousers or we'll be here all day."

"How did you know his name was Gerald?" said Felix.

"Post office," she said, as if that explained everything. It kind of did.

---

The town fountain stood in the square, splashing quietly. It was old — very old — made of grey stone with a small carved fish at the top that the water came out of. It had returned three hundred and forty-seven items. Alex knew the number. He'd counted the inscriptions on the rim, each one a different lost thing: a left glove, someone's first laugh, a Tuesday that had gone missing in 1987.

Felix crouched down and looked in. The water was very still in the middle even while it splashed around the edges. In the still part, something shimmered faintly gold.

"Hello," he said. "We've got a problem."

The water went **glug.**

"My friend's sidekick got turned into a unicorn by sticky magic," said Felix. "And we need something that's never been stuck. Do you have one?"

The fountain considered this. It had been here for a very long time. It was not in the business of rushing.

Then the water in the middle swirled, gold and bright, and pushed something up to the surface.

Alex reached in — he was always the one who reached into things like this, careful and gentle — and lifted it out.

It was a small glass bead. Perfectly smooth. Not stuck to anything, not ever. You could feel it in the way it sat in your palm — light and free and absolutely itself.

"Thank you," said Alex.

The fountain went **glug** again, which was probably goodbye.

---

Back in the field, Sergeant Sticky Pants looked at the bead doubtfully. "That's going to un-transform a unicorn?"

"You tried your way," said Felix. "Now we try ours."

He handed the bead to Alex, because it seemed right. Alex always knew what to do with small careful things.

Alex walked up to Corporal Crisp — Nigel — who had been standing in the long grass looking philosophical about everything. He held up the bead so the unicorn could see it. Nigel's big dark eyes looked at it. Then looked at Alex.

"It's okay," said Alex. "It won't stick."

He pressed the bead gently against the unicorn's nose.

There was a sound like a very large piece of toffee being pulled apart — **SCHHHHHHLUNK** — and a shimmer of gold light that went from Nigel's horn all the way down to his hooves and then

*out.*

In the long grass stood a man. Medium height. Sensible shoes. A utility belt, correctly sized. He blinked several times. He looked at his hands.

"I have hands," he said.

"Hello Nigel," said Felix.

Nigel (Corporal Crisp) looked at Felix and Alex for a long moment. Then he said, very seriously, "Thank you. Being a unicorn is magnificent but the dandelions weren't doing it for me."

Sergeant Sticky Pants made a sound that was not quite crying but was not quite not crying either. He clapped Nigel on the shoulder. Nigel's utility belt clattered cheerfully.

---

They all had biscuits.

Daddy had made tea, obviously. He'd also found some very good ones at the back of the tin — the round chocolate ones with the ridged edges — which he had been saving for a special occasion, and decided this qualified.

Sergeant Sticky Pants ate three. His trousers stuck to the chair twice, which he apologised for.

"You could come back," said Felix, through a mouthful of biscuit. "If there's another hairy adventure."

"There usually is," said the Sergeant.

"There's a fifteen-acre field," said Alex, "and a forest with a fox in it who knows everything."

Nigel, who had been listening quietly, said, "I might come back just for the fox."

---

They left as the light went golden across the field — the Sergeant's yellow cape catching the sun, Nigel's utility belt jangling — walking back through the long grass towards wherever it was that heroes went between adventures.

Felix watched them go. He had a half-eaten biscuit in his hand. He felt the good kind of full — not just biscuit-full, but *story-full*, the kind where something real had happened and you'd been part of it and now you'd remember it.

"Alex," he said.

"Yeah?"

"That was a good one."

Alex nodded. He already knew.

---

**Daddy went back inside and looked at the kitchen chair. One leg was stuck to the floor.**

**He made another cup of tea and decided it could wait until morning.**

---

*Postscripts:*

*Corporal Crisp (Nigel) returned to active duty the following Wednesday. He did not become a unicorn again, but for the rest of his career, horses found him unusually trustworthy.*

*The glass bead was returned to the fountain the next time Felix and Alex passed it. The fountain gave them back one left glove (slightly damp) and a Tuesday from 1987, which turned out to be quite a nice one.*

*The toffee trousers eventually released the kitchen chair. This took eleven days. Robert did not mention it. Magda mentioned it once, in Polish, while making soup. This was sufficient.*

*Sergeant Sticky Pants left his number, written on a piece of card that smelled faintly of butterscotch. Felix put it on the evidence shelf between the bark note from the rook and Arthur's Mondays. It seemed right.*

---

*[END]*


===STORY===

# Trio Force: Case File #33 — The Wishing Pest

```meta
id: trio-force-case-file-33-the-wishing-pest
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.619
scores: affirm 2.51 / emotion 4.66 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 4.46
words: 1391
minutes: ~10
date: 2026-05-13
source_chat: Monkey's paw powers for Alex, Felix, and Amelia
source_uuid: 844dc6f8-2e85-4985-a10a-8eae28b1dee2
prompt: new story, Alex Felix Amelia, this time they get to choose the most suitable power to solve a problem/challenge/obstacle/villain/etc, BUT they are like monkeys paw powers and get t
reviewed: auto-scored (confirm on read)
elevenlabs_status: not yet recorded
```

## Story

The box arrived on a Tuesday, which was unusual.

Boxes usually came on Saturdays. Gold ones, on the best Saturdays. But this one appeared on the HQ doorstep on an ordinary Tuesday morning, and it wasn't gold at all. It was purple, with a small silver tag that read:

*For when you need to think carefully about what you actually want.*

Felix picked it up immediately. Alex read the tag twice.

"I don't love the sound of that," said Amelia, who had her notebook open already.

Inside the box were three smaller boxes — one red, one blue, one green — each with a little dial on the front, like a safe. And on the inside of the lid, written in very neat, very small letters:

*Choose your power. Turn the dial. The power is yours — exactly as requested. Read the small print.*

There was no small print.

"That's worrying," said Amelia.

"BRILLIANT," said Felix, and reached for the red one.

---

They needed the powers because of the Wishing Pest.

The Wishing Pest — real name unknown, height approximately four feet, wearing a large coat with far too many pockets — had appeared in town three days ago. It didn't steal things. It didn't break things. What it did was considerably worse.

It granted wishes.

Not nicely. Not helpfully. In the way that made you think for a moment you'd got exactly what you wanted, and then realise you absolutely hadn't.

Mr. Pemberton the baker had wished for more customers. He now had *far* too many customers, a queue that went around the block, and had run out of flour on Monday. Mrs. Okafor at the post office had wished for a quieter day. Every parcel, letter, and package in the entire county had been redirected somewhere else, and the post office was now completely, eerily silent, and she couldn't send anything either.

The town fountain — which, as Trio Force knew, was very important — had stopped working entirely. The keeper was very upset. Someone had wished the fountain would be more impressive, and it now shot water forty feet into the air, which was spectacular and also meant nobody could get near it.

"We need to get close enough to catch the Pest," said Amelia, spreading her notes on the HQ desk. "It's fast. It disappears into crowds. And every time someone approaches it, it just offers them a wish, and things get worse."

"I want to fly," said Felix immediately, hand on the red box.

Alex looked at him. "It says read the small print."

"There IS no small print."

"That," said Alex quietly, "is the small print."

Felix turned the dial on the red box anyway.

There was a soft FWUMP, and Felix rose two inches off the floor, hovered, grinned enormously — and then shot straight up and bonged his head on the ceiling of HQ.

"OW."

He could fly. Perfectly. Beautifully. Exclusively upward.

He drifted back down when he stopped thinking about it, rubbing his head. "Right," he said. "Okay. I can work with this."

Alex opened the blue box. He thought for a moment — really thought, the way he did when he was watching something the rest of them hadn't spotted yet — and said: "I want to be able to freeze things. Just for a second. So I can see them properly."

The dial turned. There was a small click.

Alex held up his hand. A bee flying past the HQ window stopped in mid-air, wings locked, a tiny perfect statue. Then it continued on its way.

"Hm," said Alex. He'd wanted to be able to freeze things to study them. The twist, he discovered a moment later, was that he could only freeze things that were *already moving*. Anything still, he couldn't touch. 

That was fine. He thought he could manage.

Amelia considered the green box for quite a long time. "I want to be understood," she said carefully. "By everyone. Whatever I say."

The dial turned.

There was a pause.

"Did it work?" said Felix.

"I think so," said Amelia. She tried saying "left" and pointing right. Both boys turned left without thinking about it. She tried saying "the Pest will be near the bakery" and both boys were already heading for the door with complete certainty. She nodded. Good.

The twist arrived when she tried to say "let's be quiet" as they approached the town square, and instead of whispering it, the words came out so clearly and completely understood that they rang off every building like a bell, and the Wishing Pest — a small, quick, patchwork figure darting between the Tuesday market stalls — looked straight at them.

"Oh," said Amelia.

"THERE!" said Felix, and shot upward.

---

The chase was spectacular and almost entirely vertical.

Felix could fly after the Pest perfectly well — as long as it was going up. When the Pest ran along the ground, Felix could only hover above it like a very enthusiastic balloon, calling directions down. When it scrambled up the drainpipe of Mr. Pemberton's bakery, Felix was finally in his element and caught up immediately, grinning, rising alongside it.

The Pest looked at him. It had very small, very bright eyes.

"Wish?" it said hopefully.

"No thank you," said Felix. "We're here for a different reason."

Alex, down below, watched the Pest's coat very carefully. It kept flinching — little twitches, movement in the pockets. He raised his hand. Every pocket stopped moving at once. The Pest grabbed at its coat in confusion. The wishes inside — little glowing things, all crammed in there — were frozen mid-wriggle.

That was when Amelia stepped forward.

She spoke very carefully, very precisely, not too loud: "You need to undo the wishes you've granted today. All of them. Starting with the fountain."

The Pest heard her the way everyone heard Amelia now — with absolute, bone-deep understanding, as if the words had been said directly to the part of them that already knew it was true. Its small bright eyes went uncertain.

"They asked," said the Pest. A bit sadly.

"They didn't know what they were asking for," said Amelia. "That's the difference."

The Pest was quiet for a moment. Felix drifted gently beside it, three storeys up, saying nothing. Sometimes you didn't need to say anything.

"I just wanted to help," said the Pest eventually.

Felix nodded. "Yeah," he said. "That bit we get."

---

The wishes were undone by teatime. The fountain dropped back to its usual height. The keeper sent a small wave of approval from inside the water. Mr. Pemberton had normal quantities of customers again and looked both relieved and slightly sad about it. The parcels returned to Mrs. Okafor's post office with a sound like a flock of pigeons landing all at once.

The Wishing Pest sat in the town square and looked at its empty pockets.

"There's a group," said Felix. "Thursdays. Janet makes shortbread. You should come."

The Pest looked at its pockets again. Then at Felix.

"Is it good shortbread?"

"Classified," said Felix seriously. "But yes."

---

*End Notes:*

*Felix's flying power lasted until Thursday, which meant he got to school by going straight up over the hedge and drifting in through the playground, which he described as "the best four days of my life." He bonged his head on the school ceiling once. Just the once.*

*Alex kept his freezing power a secret for almost a week, using it exclusively to study interesting insects and once to catch a falling cup of squash before it hit the kitchen floor. Daddy noticed the squash cup and said nothing, which is his way of saying everything.*

*Amelia's power faded after forty-eight hours, which she said was "a relief, actually." Nobody was sure they believed her.*

*The Wishing Pest attended the Thursday group. It turned out to have been trying to help people for eleven years and never once getting it right. Janet gave it extra shortbread. Victor Spung let it sit next to him. It cried a little. This was considered a very good sign.*

*The three boxes went on the evidence shelf. The purple one is between Arthur's Mondays and the bark note from the rook. The dials are still set.*

*[END]*


===STORY===

# The Storm Crystal's Secret

```meta
id: the-storm-crystals-secret
tier: B
status: keeper (solid)
score: 3.608
scores: affirm 5 / emotion 1.94 / enjoy 3.2 / audio 5.0 / craft 2.2
```

## Story

Felix was practicing his red stone melody in the backyard when something strange happened. As he hummed the familiar tune, his crystal pendant started to pulse faster and faster, and suddenly he felt electricity crackling through his fingertips alongside the usual flames.

"Whoa!" he gasped, watching tiny lightning bolts dance between his fingers. This had never happened before!

Just then, a rumble of thunder echoed across the countryside, even though there wasn't a cloud in the sky. Felix looked toward the Whispering Woods and saw something incredible—a new crystal stone had appeared in the clearing, and it was glowing bright electric blue with silver streaks.

Felix raced to gather his friends, and soon they were all standing in the crystal circle, staring at the eighth stone that definitely hadn't been there last week.

"It's a Storm Crystal!" breathed Aria, watching as actual tiny lightning bolts zapped between the crystal's facets.

But as Felix approached the new stone, something went wrong. The moment he got close, all the electrical energy from his red crystal pendant started getting pulled toward the Storm Crystal like a magnet. The lightning grew wilder and wilder until—ZAP!—it shot out and struck the old oak tree at the edge of the clearing.

"Felix, step back!" called Theo. But it was too late. The Storm Crystal was drawing so much electrical energy that Felix felt stuck in place, his whole body buzzing with power he couldn't control.

The problem was getting worse. Every few seconds, another lightning bolt would shoot out randomly—hitting trees, rocks, and even creating small craters in the ground. At this rate, Felix might accidentally hurt his friends or destroy the whole forest!

"The crystal is too powerful for just the red stone song," Winter observed, staying safely back. "Felix, try combining melodies!"

Felix tried humming his red melody along with Winter's silver tune, hoping the fading power might calm the electricity. Instead, it made invisible lightning that was even more dangerous because they couldn't see where it was going!

"Not that combination!" yelped Veer as a tree branch suddenly caught fire from an invisible bolt.

Emily had an idea. "Felix, what if you try grounding the energy instead of fighting it? Use Theo's green melody!"

Felix was getting tired from all the electrical energy buzzing through him, but he took a deep breath and tried to add Theo's earth-song to his red melody. The moment he did, something amazing happened. Instead of wild, dangerous lightning, the electrical energy began flowing down through his feet into the ground in a controlled way.

But now the Storm Crystal started pulling even harder, and Felix realized what it wanted. It wasn't trying to overload him—it was trying to teach him a completely new kind of Crystal Singing. One that required him to channel massive amounts of energy safely through multiple stone songs at once.

"I think... I think I need all of you to help me learn this song!" Felix called to his friends as another controlled bolt of electricity shot safely into the ground. "This power is too big for just one person!"

His friends looked at each other, then nodded. They'd never tried to help someone else learn a new stone's song, but Felix needed them.

One by one, they began adding their melodies to Felix's red-and-green combination. Emily's golden light helped Felix see the electrical patterns more clearly. Winter's silver song helped him control which parts of the lightning stayed solid and which parts he could let fade away. Aria's purple melody let Felix mentally direct the electricity exactly where he wanted it to go. Violet's orange song created safe illusions that showed Felix what the lightning would do before he actually released it. And Veer's dark blue song helped Felix understand what the forest needed—where dead branches should be cleared with lightning, and where new growth needed the electrical energy to flourish.

Finally, Felix felt ready to actually touch the Storm Crystal. With all six of his friends singing their supportive melodies, he placed his hand on the electric blue stone.

The world exploded with power—but this time, Felix was ready. The Storm Crystal's song was wild and exciting, like music made of thunder and lightning strikes. But with his friends' help, Felix could weave it together with all the other melodies.

The result was spectacular. Felix could create lightning that healed instead of harmed, electrical energy that helped plants grow faster, and controlled storms that brought exactly the right amount of rain to exactly the right places. He could even use the electricity to power things—making Violet's light illusions brighter and more realistic, or helping Theo's plants grow in amazing spiral patterns.

But the most incredible discovery came when Felix used his new Storm Crystal song to energize his friends' powers too. When he sent gentle electrical currents through their crystal pendants, everyone's abilities became supercharged. Emily's golden light could now heal bigger injuries. Winter could make things invisible for much longer. Aria could move much heavier objects. Violet's illusions became so real they had their own smells and textures. Theo could grow entire gardens in minutes. And Veer could talk to animals from miles away.

"This is what the Storm Crystal really does," Felix realized as he finally stepped away from the eighth stone, feeling wonderfully energized instead of overwhelmed. "It doesn't just give me lightning powers. It lets me share energy with all of you, and help make everyone's Crystal Singing stronger!"

Theo grinned as he watched a magnificent tree grow from a tiny seed in just thirty seconds, powered by Felix's electrical boost. "So you're like... our team's battery now?"

Felix laughed, creating a small, gentle lightning bolt that spelled out "FELIX" in the air before safely dispersing. "More like our team's conductor! Get it? Like conducting electricity AND conducting an orchestra!"

As they headed home, Felix felt more energized than he ever had before. His new Storm Crystal abilities weren't just about having lightning powers—they were about learning to handle massive amounts of energy safely, and then using that energy to help his friends become even more amazing than they already were.

And tomorrow? Tomorrow they'd start discovering what happened when Felix energized their team combinations. He had a feeling they were about to become the most powerful group of Crystal Singers the Whispering Woods had ever seen.
